Scientiﬁc Area: I Methodology - Assays In Vivo - Genotoxicity

 
 


 

Project Name: Establishment of the Ex Vivo HPRT Assay

 

 

Objective: Establishment of an ex vivo HPRT mutation assay in rat type 11 cells as a genotoxic

to complement our PI testing battery

 

 

 

Project Leader: Weisensee, D.

 

 

Tactics and Milestones: Target Date:
     
 
  
  
   
   
   
    
   

The ex vivo genotoxicity assay (HPRT) utilizes cells that have been exposed in the
intact organism. Isolated target cells may also be useful for other endpoints (DNA
analysis, comet assay)

. Optimization of cell isolation from control rats by sub-characterization of ex vivo Mar.2000
pulmonary cells types (e.g. antibodies to surfactant proteins, alkaline phosphatase,
cytokeratins and surface antigenes)
2. Study the proliferative capacity of type 11 cell fractions to allow normalization of
mutation frequencies

J un.2000

3. Abstract submission (methodology) Sep.2000

4. Comparison and optimization of mutation expression kinetics (in vitro and in viva)
following exposure to a model mutagen (target date depends on starting time)

J un.2001
5. Planning and execution of an ex vivo positive control by instillation of rats with
quartz particles using the same strain and experimental design as in the RASS/DEE
study

Dec.2000

6. Re—evaluation of RASS/DEE study data in light of improved understanding of

psay conditions

7. Monitor literature

Mar.2001

continuous

ABSTRACT:

The current WINSTON Ligh 5 85mm is rated inferior to Marlboro
Lights 85mm among compet tive male smokers, aged 18-34. As 1 .
part of the continuing d velOpment program for WINSTON Lights 85,
two prototypes were fiel ed the week of February 28, 1983. ‘

 

 

Neither of the prototypes teeted achieved the action standard of

l

l

' superiority versus Marlb ro Li hts 85 among the competitive ~t
action standard group. in add tion, neither prototype represented
‘ a significant improvement in overall performance relative to the

current product.

Brief Summary: Temporary Procedure Note 89-28 was issued in July and provided
starting specifications for the 1989-90 stemmery season. Results to-date,
from processing of the 1989 burley crop, indicate that the starting
specifications contained in PM 89-28 are henceforth recognized as the 1989-90
Burley Processing Specification.

Action: Burley Processing Specifications as contained in PM 89-28 are
authorized by the Procedure Note 90-1, as final/permanent processing
specifications for the 1989 burley crop.

Specifications: The actual Specifications are attached. /?

ﬁndings,

Re: Hecht and Hoffmann letter draft

Dear Richard.

Following some suggestion from Hans-Juergen Haussmann, HER and others, l have
made a few minor corrections to the attached draft. However, i have also had to make
a major change in the dose/exposure calculation for NNK. Having identiﬁed the study
cited by H&H to be Belinsky et a]. (1990). the corrected PY estimate now reads 720 PY
instead of the 1.860 PY previously stated. All corrections are underlined.

AUTOMATED METHOD FOR THE DETERMINATION OF PLASTICIZERS‘
IN CIGARETTE FILTER ROD MATERIAL

‘A. J. Sensabaugh and Kenneth L. Rush, R.‘ J. Reynolds
Tobacco Company, Research Di'Vision, |l5 Chestnut Street,
‘ Winston-Salem, North Carolina, 27lOl ‘ - \

An automated method is proposed for the colorimetric determination of triacetin and
riethyleneglycol diacetate plasticizers in cellulose acetate cigarette filter rods.

Should the identity of the plasticizer be unknown. initial testing must include a

Aimple qualitative analysis by GC. Sample preparation consists'of~.extra'ction of
Then the reaction of the extracted

nlasticizer from the filter material with methanol.
-cetate with hydroxylamine, followed by an-addition of ferric chloride, yields a
The absorption maximum of the

- erric hydroxamate complex, producing a violet color. _
omplex is at 500 nm and follows Beer‘s Law from 0-800 ug/ml. The optical density range

'5 moo-0.700.

The Simplicity of this procedure lends itself well to use with automated instrumenta-
ion. It has"'been ada ted for use on the Robot Chemist which permits the performance of
- -nalyses at a rate of 20 per hour. less the standards necessary for a concentration
k equally well for either triacetin or~triethylene;
urve. The methodhas been shown to-wor
-lycol. diacetate, after selection of the appropriate standard for use in construction of

RE: Junk Science Column, D. Post.

# ongs: 2

We’ve got the ball rolling out here on the junk science issue! Pls. refer to the attached
column written by editorial writer & columnist Al Knight of the Mimicking
the EPA’s methodology and science with their new Clean Air Standards.
One of Al’s growing pet peeves is the assumption by some governmental agencies of new
powers to establish guidelines over previously exempt industries, products and domains,

without regard to need or cosr-beneﬁr analyses.

We believe it may be a short step for Al to delve into junk science as an ongoing topic for
his thrice-weekly column, since there are several local situations that can be bolstered with
broader, national information. We are assembling materials to assist him in criticizing the
wrong—headcdnoss of the EPA, FDA, OSHA and other bureaucracies that are apparently
expanding their empires via rules and regulations they may not actually have the authority
to implement.
